# Microsoft 365 Teams Administrator Associate Cert Prep Ms 700 Plan Configure And Deploy

> Organizations around the world have adopted Microsoft Teams for its secure conferencing, chat, and collaboration features. Employers need certified administrators to deploy, manage, and monitor the platform. Luckily, to achieve the Microsoft Teams Administrator Associate certification, you only need to pass one exam: MS-700 Managing Microsoft Teams. This course, the first of a two-part series, hel

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy) | Intermediate | 7K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=8)** First one might be jitter, and that describes the occurrence where the media arrives at different rates, which results in missing words or syllables in your calls.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=19)** And another would be packet loss.

> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=39)** What will happen is the users will experience noticeable delays between both parties in a conversation, and that can cause people to end up speaking at the same time.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=48)** To provide Quality of Service, network devices are going to need to have a way to classify traffic and be able to tell the difference between voice or video from other network traffic.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=59)** When the network traffic passes through a router, it's placed in what's called a queue.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=64)** If a QoS policy is not configured, there's going to be just one queue and all traffic will be treated with the same priority.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=71)** So what we need to do is to implement QoS.

> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=74)** And you can define multiple queues using one of several congestion management features and congestion avoidance features.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=82)** We're going to need to verify your network is ready for QoS.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=86)** Using QoS requires all network devices to be managed.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=90)** Unmanaged devices, such as simple layer two switches, cannot take advantage of Quality of Service, so you need to use layer three.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=97)** If an organization's network is unmanaged and does not support QoS, it may be required to replace some of the network devices in order to get proper support.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=107)** There are different methods for implementation of QoS.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=110)** The first one is access control lists.

> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=113)** You can implement QoS via port-based tagging.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=117)** This is where we tag the ports on the layer three switch, as an example, using access control lists on your network routers and switches.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=125)** Port-based tagging is the most reliable method because it's going to work universally throughout all platforms.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=131)** So it doesn't matter which brand of quality product that you have, such as Cisco or Dell, HP, and others, they'll all work along with your [[Windows]] and Mac environments, and it's also the easiest to implement.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=146)** The other option is going to be group policy object, and this happens when you implement QoS by using a group policy object in Windows to direct client devices to insert a differentiated services code point, or DSCP marker, in the IP packet headers.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=161)** We also need to choose initial port ranges for each media type.

>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/configure-media-optimizations-by-using-qos?u=76281980&t=173)** We need to implement QoS in the Teams Admin Center.

> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/required-licensing-for-compliance-features?u=76281980&t=37)** There's office 365 licenses that you'll need to purchase: E5, A5 or G5, and there's also Microsoft 365 licenses.

> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/required-licensing-for-compliance-features?u=76281980&t=46)** The Microsoft and Office 365 licenses, although they show up as two different types, are actually the same licenses.

> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=89)** Now we have the option for Select Record Type.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=91)** So I'll hit the dropdown, and I'll choose [[Microsoft Teams]], and now we can see the results of all activities.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=103)** So we see the option for Created and Deleted Team, and we could do other things such as add a channel, delete a channel, et cetera.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=110)** Once we have it the way we want it, we need to choose the duration, and that could be 90 days all the way up to 10 years.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=117)** And if there's a priority, we can enter that as well.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=120)** I'm going to make it Priority 1, and click Save.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=124)** Now I only have one audit retention policy, so it doesn't really matter which priority I have.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=129)** But if you have multiple in there, then you're going to want to choose the priority that you want it to search.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=134)** Now when you create or delete a team in Microsoft Teams, this audit policy, first off, takes about an hour before it will kick in; and then it can take 10 to 15 minutes before you're going to start seeing any types of results after someone creates or deletes a team.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-teams-administrator-associate-cert-prep-ms-700-plan-configure-and-deploy/monitor-and-report-on-creation-and-deletion-of-teams?u=76281980&t=150)** Creating an audit policy for team creation and deletion has been moving around a lot from the Teams admin center and the 365 admin center, so be sure to check Microsoft's latest documentation before setting up the alert in the compliance center.
